From this it is evident that one gets all happiness only when he is capable of using the right word in the right place. This suggests that only such persons will be chosen to officiate as priests. This can be done only with the knowledge of grammar. Hence grammar helps BrƒÅhma·πáas to get fees in the sacrifices and success elsewhere. ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§É- ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•á ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§®‡•ã ‡§Ø‡•á ‡§® ‡§™‡•ç‡§≤‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§É ‡•§

[[1]]

‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§§‡•Å ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡•ç ‡•• ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç [ ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§É ] Those illiterate persons who do not know that pluti (the use of three matras) must be made use of while blessing a man who prostrates, must be prostrated in the same way as women after one returns to his place after some time and be told by him that he is such by name. Grammar is to be studied lest we should be treated like women in abhivadana. From this we learn that knowledge of grammar is needed to keep up one’s dignity as a learned Brahmana. ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø- ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‚Äú ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É " ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§® ‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§É ‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ [‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ] Chapters dealing with sacrifices read that the prayƒÅja mantras should be recited with the proper cases. But for the knowledge of grammar, it is not possible to do. Prayajas are the subsidiary h≈çmas in the Darsapur·πáamasa sacrifice. It is a duty enjoined by the Vedas to be performed by a house-holder in the same way as sthalipaka enjoined by the Sm·πõtis to be performed by the same person. Even though the mantras for prayƒÅja h≈çmas are completely read, yet he is allowed to perform an i·π£ti if the yajamƒÅna is attacked of stomach-ache after adhana or meets with a great disaster within a year, where the deity to be invoked is Agni. Hence while performing it, he is to change the mantras in such a way as to suit it. This is the same as the mentioned before. Hence it is clear that the second set of prayojanas mentioned is quotation from previous author or authors. 32 PASPASAHNIKA ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç- ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§¶‡§∂‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§∂‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§∂‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏ ‡§Ü‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•Ä‡§®‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ü‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•• He who is capable of pronouncing the mantras correctly with respect to words, accent and letters is fit to become a sacrificer or to officiate as priest in sacrifices. Grammar is to be studied so that we may be qualified to become priests or to perform sacrifices. The word ‡§Ü‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•Ä‡§®‡§É means a sacrificer if it is split as ‡§ã‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§§‡§ø on the strength of the sutra ‡§Ø‡§∂‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ò‡§ñ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä (P.). It means a priest if it is split as ‡§ã‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§§‡§ø on the strength of the VƒÅrttika ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§™‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç. This is also more or less the same as mentioned in ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∂‡§≤‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡•á etc. ‡§ö‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø- ‡§ö‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø ‡§∂‡•É‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•á ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§ ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ ‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã ‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡§≠‡•ã ‡§∞‡•ã‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡•ã ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Ü‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§∂ || ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ö‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø ‡§∂‡•É‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§ö‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø ‡§™‡§¶‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ã‡§™‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§®‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡•§ ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§É‚Äî‚Äî-‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§É, ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§≠‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§É ‡•§ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§∂‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡•á ‚Äî ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•å ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•å, ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡•§ ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§ ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø - ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ ‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§É, ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§É, ‡§â‡§∞‡§∏‡§ø ‡§ï‡§£‡•ç‡§†‡•á ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§µ‡•É‡§∑‡§≠‡•ã, ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§∞‡•ã‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø, ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§ ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç ? ‡§∞‡•å‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡•§ ‡§Æ‡§π‡•ã ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Ü‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§É, ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§É ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É, ‡§Æ‡§∞‡§£‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ; ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§Ü‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§∂ ‡•§ ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•á‡§® ‡§®‡§É ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•• The Vrsabha which has four horns, three feet, two heads and seven hands and which is bound in three places cries 33

[[5]]

that the Great God entered the mortals. The four horns-the four parts of speech-noun, verb, upasarga (preposition) and nipata. Its three feet-the three tenses, past, future and present. Two heads-the two kinds of sabda, nitya (eternal) and karya (non-eternal). Its seven hands-the seven cases. It is bound three-fold-It is bound at three placeschest, neck and head. The word vrsabha is derived from the root vrs (4). The word reffa means ‘makes noise.’ Whence is it? The root means to make noise. The Great God entered the mortals-the Great God is sabda; the word H: literally means mortals and hence men; He entered them, Grammar is to be studied so that we may become one with the Great God. ‡§Æ‡§π‡•ã ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§É here refers to ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ. It has already been mentioned that Indian Grammarians recognise four phases of speech-sound, of which is considered to be nitya and the other three ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä, ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ and ‡§µ‡•à‡§ñ‡§∞‡•Ä are kƒÅrya. The word arfa in the BhƒÅ·π£ya text refers, in the opinion of Nag≈çji Bhatta, to the four phases of speech-sound, since, otherwise at the end dedaqar: cannot be appropriate. But from the following reading of Nirukta ‡§ö‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø ‡§™‡§¶‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•á ‡§ö‡•ã‡§™‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§®‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö I think MahƒÅbhƒÅsyakƒÅra also may have had the same reading. Though upasargas are only nipatas at a particular setting, yet they have been mentioned following the maxim called ‡§ó‡•ã‡§¨‡§≤‡•Ä‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø. ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç is interpreted by NƒÅg≈çji Bhatta to refer to on the strength of the Karika of Bhart·πõhari, ‡§Ö‡§™‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•É‡§∑‡§≠‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡•• The Rkaf…is the third Rk in the 58th Sukta of the fourth mandala in Rgvƒìda. SƒÅya·πáƒÅcƒÅrya, in his BhƒÅ·π£ya, 34 PASPASƒÄHNIKA says that since the presiding deity of this Rk is one of five deities, this Rk is interpreted in five ways : Cf. ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ö‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ß‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§É ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§ï‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§® ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§§‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á … The same Rk is commented upon in Yaska’s Nirukta XIII, 1-7. The expression ‡§ö‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø, MahƒÅbhƒÅsyakƒÅra says, is taken by others to refer to the following Rk. This clearly shows that this set of prayojanas was in vogue long before the time of MahƒÅbhƒÅ·π£yakƒÅra. ‡§Ö‡§™‡§∞ ‡§Ü‡§π- ‡§ö‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•á ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§É ‡•§ ‡§ó‡•Å‡§π‡§æ ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§£‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§®‡•á‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§µ‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡•§

‡§ö‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ö‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø ‡§™‡§¶‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø, ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ã‡§™‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§®‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡•§ ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•á ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏ ‡§à‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡•ã, ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§É ‡•§ ‡§ó‡•Å‡§π‡§æ ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§£‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§®‡•á‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø, ‡§ó‡•Å‡§π‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§£‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§®‡•á‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø, ‡§® ‡§ö‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á, ‡§® ‡§®‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∑‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•§ ‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§µ‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§è‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•á ‡§ö‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•• ‡§ö‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø ‡•• Others say :- There are four kinds of speech-sound, which are seen by those BrƒÅhma·πáas who have controlled their mind. Three of them are not cognizable since they are inside the body. Men speak out only the fourth. The four kinds of speech-sound-the four kinds are noun, verb, upasarga and nipƒÅta. They are seen by manisins-manisins are those who have controlled their mind.

[[5]]

Three do not exhibit themselves being kept in guha-three are kept in guha-the meaning of a is, they do not operate (i.e.) exhibit. Men speak out the fourth-that which is among men is the fourth phase of the speech-sound.
The same Rk is commented upon in Yaska’s Nirukta XIII. 1. 9., where rf rf is explained thus:-
‡§ö‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø ‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ì‡§Ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§π‡§æ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π‡•É‡§§‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•, ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•á ‡§ö ‡§â‡§™‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§®‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡•à‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡§æ‡§É, ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§É ‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡•ã ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•ã ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§É, ‡§ã‡§ö‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•Ç‡§Ç‡§∑‡§ø ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ö‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•ã ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡•à‡§∞‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡•§ etc.
It means this:-
The four padas are, in the opinion of seers, pra·πáava and three vyah·πõtis; they are, in the opinion of grammarians, noun, verb, upasarga and nipata; etc.; according to sacrificers they are mantra, kalpa, brahmana and the fourth that is in vogue; they according to Nairuktas, are Rk, yajus, Saman and those that are in vogue. It appears as the 45th Rk in 164th Sukta of the first Mandala in Rgveda. SƒÅya·πáa in his commentary mentions in addition to what has been mentioned in Nirukta,
‡§Ö‡§™‡§∞‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§æ ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§µ‡•à‡§ñ‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§ö‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø ‡•§
Other mƒÅntrikas think that the four are (‡§™‡§∞‡§æ, ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä, ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ and ‡§µ‡•à‡§ñ‡§∞‡•Ä). Nagoji Bhatta explains ‡§™‡§¶‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø thus :-‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§µ‡•à‡§ñ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡§ø ‡§ö‡•§ He seems to have added ‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä-
since it is said that three of them are not cognizable and since it was recognised by grammarians that, of the four phases of speech-sound, ‡§™‡§∞‡§æ, ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä and ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ are not cognizable to those other than Y√∂gins. 36 PASPASAHNIKA ‡§â‡§§ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§É ‡§â‡§§ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§É ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡§¶‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§É ‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§â‡§§‡•ã ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à ‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡§≤‡•á ‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§â‡§∂‡§§‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§É ‡•• ‡•§‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§ø ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§ï‡§É ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§™‡§ø ‡§® ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§™‡§ø ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§ï‡§É ‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§™‡§ø ‡§® ‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç; ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§â‡§§‡•ã ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à ‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡§≤‡•á ‡§§‡§®‡•Å‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§£‡•Å‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§â‡§∂‡§§‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§É - ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ, ‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§£‡•Å‡§§‡•á‡•§ ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•á ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§£‡•Å‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§®‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§£‡•Å‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•• ‡§â‡§§ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§É ‡•• One, though he sees vale (speech), does not see her; one, though he hears her, does not hear her. Thus the first half of the stanza speaks of one who is not learned in grammar. She discloses her body to some one in the same way as a lady opens herself to her husband when she is in clean dress and wants his company. So speech opens herself to the grammarian. In order that vak may open herself to us, grammar is to be studied. The word a means though’ and the word : means ‚Äòone.’ ‘The expression ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§™‡§ø ‡§® ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§Æ‡•ç means though he sees, he does not see speech.’ The word a qualifies ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç and not ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§É. The expression ‡§Ö‡§™‡§ø ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§ï‡§É ‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§™‡§ø ‡§® ‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç means though one hears, he does not hear her. The word ‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç is the earlier form of ‡§§‡§®‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç (which means body). The word ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á means ‘discloses. The expression ‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§â‡§∂‡§§‡•Ä ‡§∏‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§É means it is like the wife who, being in clean dress and eager to meet her husband, opens herself. The word may here be taken to mean both mind and body. (The body and mind of vak is evidently her meaning). It is clear that the latter half of the stanza speaks of the learned grammarian.

[[7]]

The word in two places and in the latter half suggest that one in, say, hundred takes to study grammar, one in, say, thousand studies to understand it, and one in, say, ten thousand or so is able to completely master it. The word ‡§∏‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§É suggests, as is stated in YƒÅska’s Nirukta, that she is in her rtukala. ·πötukala is the period of sixteen days beginning with the commencement of her monthly period and it, excluding the first three or four days, is considered to be the period of conception. It deserves to be noted that the injunction ‡§ã‡§§‡•å ‡§â‡§™‡•á‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç (one should meet his wife in Rtukala) found in Dharmasutras is taken to be a niyama-vidhi for those who have not given birth to a son; (i.e.) if they do not meet their wives in that period, they will meet with demerit. This R: ‚Äú‡§â‡§§ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§É… ‡§∏‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§É " is found in the Rgveda as the fourth Rk in the 71st sukta of the 10th Mandala. In commenting upon it Saya·πáƒÅcƒÅrya explains the following words. thus :- ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§™‡§ø - ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§æ ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ö‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§™‡§ø ‡§® ‡§¶‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂ ‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§®‡§´‡§≤‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§â‡§∂‡§§‡•Ä - ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡•ã‡§ó‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ The same Rk is commented upon in Nirukta (I. 6. 3) thus :- ‡§Ö‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§ï‡§É ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§ø ‡§ö ‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡•ç ‚Äî ‡§Ö‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à ‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§£‡•Å‡§§‡•á ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§®‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π‡§æ‡§®‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•ã‡§™‡§Æ‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ ‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á, ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§ã‡§§‡•Å‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§∏‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§ã‡§§‡•Å‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§∏ ‡§è‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏ ‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ || 38 ‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§ø‡§µ ‚Äî PASPASAHNIKA ‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§ø‡§µ ‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§â‡§®‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§Æ‡§ï‡§§ ‡•§

‡§Ö‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§∏‡§ñ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§§‡•á ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø ‡••

‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§É ‡§∏‡§ö‡§§‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø, ‡§ï‡§∏‡§§‡•á‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§â ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡§µ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§§‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ, ‡§§‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡•§ ‡§ß‡•Ä‡§∞‡§æ‡§É ‚Äî ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡•§ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§Æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§§-

‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§Æ‡§ï‡•Ç‡§∑‡§§ ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§∏‡§ñ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§§‡•á ‚Äì ‡§Ö‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§∏‡§ñ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§, ‡§∏‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§ï‡•§ ‡§Ø ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•á ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§É ‡§è‡§ï‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§ï‡•á ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ? ‡§µ‡•à‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡§æ‡§É ‡•§ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§ ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç ? ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•à‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø ‡§è‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§¢‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡•• ‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§ø‡§µ ‡•• Where learned men sift correct words from incorrect ones through knowledge as people the flour of barley meal through sieve, there they, being friends of words or having unblemished knowledge throughout are able to see the true meaning; for the propitious Goddess Laksmi resides in their speech. The word ‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§É is derived from the root ‡§∏‡§ö‡•ç and hence literally means that which can be cleaned only with difficulty. Or it is derived from the root, has by metathesis, assumed this form and means that which is spread.’ The word faas means ‘sieve’ and it is so since it is wide or perforated. The word fr: means learned men.’ The word ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§æ means ’through knowledge. The expression ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§Æ‡§ï‡§§ means ‚Äòmade words’ (i.e.) sifted correct words from incorrect ones. In the expression ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§ñ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§§‡•á the word ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É is understood after ‡§∏‡§ñ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§Ö‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ is lengthened to ‡§Ö‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ for the sake of metre. Where ? (i.e.) to which place does the word a refer? That which is difficult of access and which can be achieved only through speech. Who are they ? (i.e.) to whom does the word : refer? Grammarians. Why is ‡§∏‡§ñ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É

it so? For the propitious Goddess Laksmi resides in their speech. The word Lak·π£mi is derived from the root laks which means to shine and hence she becomes the lord. This Rk is found in the Rgv√©da as the second Rk of 71st sukta of the 10th Mandala and it is commented upon in Yaska’s Nirukta (IV. 2. 1 & 2). The expression ‡§∏‡§ñ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø a is interpreted in different ways. (2) They being friends, get the fruits to be obtained by the knowledge of speech. ‡§∏‡§ñ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§É ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§É, ‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§§‡•á ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø, ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§ñ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ ‡§¨‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∏‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§≤‡§≠‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡•• (S√°yana) DurgƒÅcƒÅrya, the commentator on Nirukta interprets it thus: they having the same knowledge as others are able to gauge the merits of their partners. Cf. ‡§∏‡§ñ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§É ‡§§‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•á ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à‡§ï‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§≠‡•á‡§¶‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§É ‡•• NƒÅg≈çji Bha·π≠·π≠a is of opinion that the rks ‡§ö‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø ‡§∂‡•É‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ…. ‡§ö‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§â‡§§ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§É and ‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡§ø‡§µ show that the study of grammar enables one to attain m≈çksa. 40 PASPASƒÄHNIKA ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‚Äú‡§Ü‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§™‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•á‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•• ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•• Scriptures dealing with sacrifices read thus:-If a householder performing agnihotra mispronounces a word, he will have to perform an expiatory ceremony (i·π£ti) called sarasvati isti. In order that we may not be put to the necessity of performing expiatory ceremonies, grammar is to be studied. ‡§¶‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø- ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‚Äî ‚Äú‡§¶‡§Ç‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç ‡§ò‡•ã‡§∑‡§µ‡§¶‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ‡§®‡•Ç‡§ï‡§Æ‡§®‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§ø‡§§‡§§‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç” ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§® ‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•• ‡§¶‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡•• Scriptures dealing with sacrifices read thus:- On the day following the tenth from the birth of a son, a name should be given to him. The name should have for its initial a voiced letter, should have the semi-vowels in the middle, should not have a vrddhi letter as the first of its vowels, should have been current within three generations and should not be one very popular among his enemies’ families. Only such a name enables him to have long life, success in life etc. It should contain two or four letters, should be made of a stem and a primary suffix and not a secondary suffix. Without the knowledge of grammar one does not know whether a suffix is primary or secondary. A *This is the meaning given by the Mahabha·π£yak√°ra to the expression ‡§¶‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø found in Dharmas’astras. 41

study of Dharmasutras enables one to understand that the expression ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ is ‡§â‡§™‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£ and should be taken to mean even number of letters. The word means palate. The word ‡§ï‡§æ‡§ï‡•Å‡§É means tongue. Since the tongue acts upon the palate, ‚Üë ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç is another reading. Considering ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≤‡•á‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Æ, ‡§¶‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡§π‡§ø… ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ is the better reading. 42 PASPASAHNIKA it is called ‡§ï‡§æ‡§ï‡•Å‡§¶‡§Æ‡•ç. Just as fire from within & perforated well-made iron image spirts out, so also the seven caseoceans spirt out of your palate. Hence you are satyadeva. Grammar is to be studied so that we may become satyadevas. This Rk is the 12th Rk of the 58th sukta of the eighth Mandala in Rgvƒìda. SƒÅya·πáƒÅcƒÅrya in his commentary takes the word fera: to mean rivers. The same Rk is commented upon in Nirukta V. 4-9. ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡§ø‡§ó‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ú‡§®‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á, ‡§® ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡§™‡§ø ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç ? ‡§ì‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∂‡§É ‡§∂‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡•• Why is the enumeration of benefits accruing from the study of Vyakarana alone made and not from that of any other (like the study of the Vedas etc.) ? They say ‘≈çm’ and begin to repeat chapter by chapter the Vedic words commencing from ‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç. ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™ ‡§è‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‚Äî ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§æ ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ß‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§§‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§É ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ ‡§â‡§™‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§§‡§¶‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§® ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡•§ ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§Æ‡§ß‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§É ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§É, ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö ‡§≤‡•å‡§ï‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§É, ‡§Ö‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡•á‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•É‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡•Å‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡•ç ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ü‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•á ‡§á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡•• Annambhatta in his uddyotona says that the correct reading is ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç and it governs ‡§™‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø so that it means thoroughly (i.e.) in such a way that they can be pronounced without another’s help. Cf. ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç, ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ß‡•Ä‡§®‡•ã‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡§£‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§™‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡•§ ‡§è‡§§‡•á‡§® ‘‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§æ‡§†‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§ø‡§ï‡§É, ‘‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∂‡§É ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡§æ‡§†‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç. Bharthari in his Pradipika seems to have preferred ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§É to ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∂‡§É Cf. ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡§ø‡§É ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∂‡§É ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§æ‡§†‡§É and takes that ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§ means ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§™‡§æ‡§†‡§ï. ‚Ä†The word : is omitted in some editions.

[[3]]

This was in the old Kalpa that the Brahma·πáas studied grammar after their upanayana. The Vedas were then taught to them who had a knowledge of the place of production and the effort, internal and external, of sounds. But now it is not so. After studying the Vedas, they hasten to become teachers thinking that, since they know Vedic words from the study of the Vedas and the laukika words from their contact with the world, the study of grammar is unnecessary. The AcƒÅrya (MahƒÅbhƒÅsyakƒÅra) out of affection towards such scholars with wrong notions, narrates this portion containing the benefits accruing from the study and hence the need of the study of Grammar. ‡§â‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§É ‡•§ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§Æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡•• (The classification of) word has been said; its definition has been given and the benefits have been narrated. ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç, ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•ã‡§™‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É, ‡§Ü‡§π‡•ã‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§™‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•ã‡§™‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§É, ‡§Ü‡§π‡•ã‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç ‡§â‡§≠‡§Ø‡•ã‡§™‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§É ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ! S’abdanusƒÅsana is now to be expounded. How should it be done? Is a list of correct words to be given, or a list of incorrect words; or both ? ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§∞‡•ã‡§™‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡•á‡§® ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§® ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•á‡§ß‡•ã ‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‚Äî ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡§ñ‡§æ ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É *” ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§è‡§§‡§¶‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•á‡§ß‡•á‡§® ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É ; ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§ï‡•Å‡§ü‡§É, ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Ç‡§ï‡§∞‡§É ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§è‡§§‡§¶‡•ç ‘‡§Ü‡§∞‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É’ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§π‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‚Äî ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•ã‡§™‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§É cf. ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡•ã‡§ß‡§æ‡§∂‡§∂‡§∂‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§ï‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§™‡§ñ‡§°‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§É ‡§ñ‡§°‡•ç‡§ó‡§µ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§É ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡§ñ‡§æ‡§É (Bodh. Dharma. 1-5. 131). and (Mahabharata, s’anti. 141, 70). 44 PASPAS AHNIKA ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡•á, ‡§ó‡•å‡§∞‡§ø ‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•Å‡§™‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•á, ‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§è‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§É ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§•‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•ã‡§™‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡•á, ‡§ó‡§æ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å ‡§â‡§™‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•á‡§∑‡•Å, ‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§è‡§§‡§¶‡•ç ‘‡§ó‡•å‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑ ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶ ’ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•• It is done by either method. From the injunction restricting the eatables, the non-eatables are inferred-when the injunction “Eat five five-clawed animals” is pronounced, it is inferred that all but those five animals are non-eatable. Similarly from the injunction restraining the non-eatables, the eatables are inferred. When the injunction ‘Do not eat the domestic cock and the domestic pig’ is pronounced, it is inferred that the wild cock and boar may be eaten. Similar is the case here also; if the list of correct words like it: is given, it is inferred that ref etc., are incorrect and if, on the other hand, the list of incorrect words like reft etc., is given, it may be inferred that : etc., are correct words. NOTE 1. ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡§ñ‡§æ ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É - Is this ‡§Ö‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§ø‡§É, ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§ø‡§É or after arfafa: ? Since there is always a craving for every one to eat anything and hence even without this injunction one may eat the flesh of the five five-clawed animals, it is not ‡§Ö‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§ø‡§É like ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§π‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡§ø. Cf. Kaiya·π≠a’s statement at farfar, ardenera. It may be taken as ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§ø‡§É like ‡§á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ó‡•É‡§≠‡•ç‡§£‡§®‡•ç ‡§∞‡§∂‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á, since by this injunction one is prevented from tasting the flesh of animals other than these five. Still Mahabha·π£yakƒÅra takes it to be a fafafa: since it also wards off one from doing what is not mentioned there. Cf. Nag≈çjibhatta’s statement ‡§™‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡§£‡§´‡§≤‡•ã ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§´‡§≤‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ö‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•§ ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§Ω‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∂‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡§£‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§´‡§≤‡§¨‡•ã‡§ß‡§®‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§É ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§® ‡§Ö‡§≠‡•á‡§¶‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§É‡•• NOTE 2. From Nag≈çjibha·π≠·π≠a’s statement

[[5]]

‡§Ø‡•á ‡§§‡•Å ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§™‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§¶‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§æ, ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ö ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§∏‡§æ it is clear that some scholars took to mean ‘other than five’ and ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É to mean ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É; Nagojibhatta refutes them. Among many reasons cited in support of his view, the most important is the statement of MahƒÅbhƒÅ·π£yakƒÅra himself ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§® ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•á‡§ß‡•ã ‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É ? ‡§≤‡§ò‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•ã‡§™‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§É ‡§≤‡§ò‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•ã‡§™‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§É ‡§ó‡§∞‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§™‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•ã‡§™‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§É ; ‡§è‡§ï‡•à‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¨‡§π‡§µ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç‡§∂‡§æ‡§É, ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§ó‡•å‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ó‡§æ‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§ó‡•ã‡§£‡•Ä ‡§ó‡•ã‡§§‡§æ ‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡•ã‡§§‡§≤‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç‡§∂‡§æ‡§É ‡•§ ‡§á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§ø ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ Which is better? The enumeration of the correct words (is better) since it is easier - The enumeration of correct words is easier and that of incorrect words is longer; for every correct word, there are many corrupt forms. For instance the corruptions of the word ‡§ó‡•å‡§É are ‡§ó‡§æ‡§µ‡•Ä, ‡§ó‡•ã‡§£‡•Ä, ‡§ó‡•ã‡§§‡§æ, ‡§ó‡•ã‡§™‡•ã‡§§‡§≤‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ etc. We also have (another advantage of) the direct enumeration of the words that we require. NOTE 3. The second reason given above suggests that the list of corrupt forms cannot enable us to understand the correct form of a word. ‡§Ö‡§•‡•à‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•ã‡§™‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡•á ‡§∏‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•å ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§¶‡§™‡§æ‡§†‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É, ‡§ó‡•å‡§É, ‡§Ö‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§É, ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§É, ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä, ‡§∂‡§ï‡•Å‡§®‡§ø‡§É, ‡§Æ‡•É‡§ó‡§É, ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§É ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§®‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π, ‡§Ö‡§®‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•å ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§¶‡§™‡§æ‡§†‡§É ‡•§ ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‚Äî‚Äî ‡§¨‡•É‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§¶‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ ’ ‡•§ ‡§¨‡•É‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ, ‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§Ö‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§æ, ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§®‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡§É ‡§® ‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§ó‡§æ‡§Æ ‡•§ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§•‡§æ ‡§ö‡§ø‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏ ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§∂‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ; ‡§ö‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡•å‡§∞‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§â‡§™- 9

  • ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§•‡§É (Pradipika) ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§É ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡•á (Pradipa) 46 …. PASPAS AHNIKA ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ü‡§ó‡§Æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á‡§®, ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á‡§®, ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ö‡§®‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á‡§® ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á‡§® ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§ö ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ü‡§ó‡§Æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§Ü‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§™‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§®‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•å ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§¶‡§™‡§æ‡§†‡§É ‡•• When it has thus been decided that the list of correct words is to be given, there arises the question whether an inventory of all available correct words should be taken. Are we to enumerate words like ‡§ó‡•å‡§É, ‡§Ö‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§É, ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä, ‡§∂‡§ï‡•Å‡§®‡§ø‡§É, :: etc.? ‘No’ says he, for such a list is not an easy means to learn correct words.’ Thus runs a story in scriptures-B·πõhaspati (the preceptor of the gods) taught Indra the work called S’abdaparayana containing all available correct words for thousand divine years, but could not exhaust it; B·πõhaspati is the teacher, Indra is the student, the period of instruction is thousand divine years and still it was not possible to come to an end. When such is the case, how is it possible now? He who, after all, lives longest, lives hundred summers; Vidya is used in four ways in a man’s life-time; it is learnt at the feet of the guru, it is revised, it is taught to a student and it is made use of in practical life (as in sacrifices etc.). If one attempts to learn at the feet of a guru the list of all correct words, his whole life-time will be used only in learning. Hence pratipadapatha is not an easy means to get at the knowledge of correct words. ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø ‡§á‡§Æ‡•á ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ? ‡§ï‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§µ‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç, ‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§Ö‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡•á‡§® ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡§É ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•å‡§ò‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∞‡§®‡•ç ‡•• How then are the correct words to be learnt? Some work formulating general and special rules should be written *The word is not found in some editions.

so that people can with a little effort learn the vast ocean of words. ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç ? ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§™‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡•å‚Äî ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡§™‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§É ‡•§ ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§ï‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§É ? ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É, ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‘‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§£‡•ç ’ ; ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡•á‡§£‡§æ‡§™‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§É, ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‘‡§Ü‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•Å‡§™‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•á ‡§ï‡§É ’ ‡•• What is it? General rules and exceptions: some general rule is to be formulated and some exception. How is the general rule to be framed and how the exception? General rule which is to apply to things in general, like is to be read and so are exceptions to apply to some special things among them like ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•Å‡§™‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•á ‡§ï‡§É NOTE. The sutra means that, if in a compound the verb is preceded by the object which qualifies it, the suffix ‡§Ö‡§£‡•ç follows the verb; ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•Å‡§™‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•á ‡§ï‡§É means that, if the verb mentioned above ends in a and is not preceded by a preposition, it takes the suffix ‡§ï. VI Having thus decided that Grammar formulating general rules and exceptions is necessary to enable one to understand correct words, MahabhƒÅ·π£yakƒÅra discusses briefly whether the meaning of words is ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§ø (genus) or ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§ø (species) and whether the words are nitya or kƒÅrya. ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡§æ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É, ‡§Ü‡§π‡•ã‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§â‡§≠‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π ‡•§ ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ? ‡§â‡§≠‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§£ ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§™‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ü‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‘‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§µ‡§ö‡§®‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç’ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‘‡§∏‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§ï‡§∂‡•á‡§∑ ‡§è‡§ï‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•å ’ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§ï‡§∂‡•á‡§∑ ‡§Ü‡§∞‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡•• Does a word connote genus or species? Both ’ says he. How is it? For, sutras conceding both the views are written 48 PASPAS AHNIKA by the Acarya (Panini). The sutra arenenfen is read on the idea that the connotation of the word is genus and the sutra … is read on the idea that it is individuality. NOTE. It is worth noting that genus cannot exist without vyakti and the latter cannot without the former. Still there are two classes of schools, one holding that word connotes only genus and vyakti comes along with it, and the other holding that word connotes only vyakti since the former cannot exist away from the latter. But the Acarya Panini clearly shows in his work that he holds both the views, one in one context and the other in another. ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§É, ‡§Ü‡§π‡•ã‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É : ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§¶‡•ã‡§∑‡§æ‡§É, ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑ ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§Ø‡§É ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§Ö‡§•‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É, ‡§â‡§≠‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•• Is sabda nitya or karya? This was examined in detail in the work Sangraha whether sabda is eternal or noneternal. Merits and demerits on both sides were mentioned. This is the conclusion arrived at there, that, irrespective of sabda being nitya or karya, grammar is to be written. NOTE. Sangraha is a work written by Vyadi in 100,000 verses. It is unfortunate that the work is almost lost. MahƒÅbhƒÅ·π£yakara has already suggested that, if sabda refers to sphota, it is nitya and that, if it refers to dhvani-the sound that is produced by the vocal organs-it is kƒÅrya. is another reading.

Cf. ‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡•ã‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•Ç‡§≤‡§ï‡§ï‡•Å‡§¶‡§ñ‡•Å‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡§æ‡§£‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏ ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§É ‡§Ö‡§•‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§ï‡•ã ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á ‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡§ø‡§É ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§É ‡•• VII Having now decided that a should be written, MahƒÅbhƒÅ·π£yakƒÅra may have dealt with the topic-the meaning of cum. Without doing it, he deals with the purpose served by . The reason for doing so is that he wants to observe in the discussion of topics, the order followed by the Varttikakara, since his Bhasya is an elaborate commentary on not only Panini’s sutras but also on Katyayana’s varttikas. ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡§ø‡§®‡•á‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç " How has the Acarya Panini proceeded in his work? This serves as an introduction to the first varttika which runs as follows:- ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É, ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§≤‡•å‡§ï‡§ø‡§ï‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡•• When word, its meaning and their relation (or word and the relation with its meaning) are learnt to be nitya from the world and word is used only in such meanings as are current there, the sastra enjoins (the use of correct words) for the sake of dharma as in the case of incidents, laukika and vaidika. Prabhat Chandra Chakravarti translates this in the Indian Historical Quarterly Vol. I, 1925 thus:-Why, again, the grammatical treatise of the venerable Panini has been made? (If words are held to be eternal, what is the use of grammar?) Since the previous sentence is, the legitimate question that follows is, what doctrine Panini holds in his work. This is clear from KƒÅiyata’s statement ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§É 50 PASPASAHNIKA Here Mahabha·π£yakara deals in detail with the meanings of (1) ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•á, (2) ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É and (3) ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§É and elucidates the expressions ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§§‡§É and ‡§≤‡•å‡§ï‡§ø‡§ï‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï‡•á‡§∑‡•Å and takes ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§§‡§É twice, once along with ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á and once with ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á. ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á- ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§ø Here Mahabha·π£yakara suggests that the vigraha of ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á is ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§ö ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§è‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§É, ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§Æ‡•ç, ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§É ‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•Ä ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§É ‡•§ ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ? ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•Ç‡§ü‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§≤‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•á; ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ, ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•å‡§É ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä, ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ Now what is the meaning of the word fer? It is the synonym of the word nitya. How is it so? Since it is used along with objects which do not move and which do not change. Ex. ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•å‡§É (the Heaven is nitya), ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä (the earth is nitya) and ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç (the sky is nitya). NOTE. The expressions fear at: etc., are not based upon the conception that ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•å‡§É ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä etc., are eternal, but upon the conception that they are relatively permanent.* MahƒÅbhƒÅ·π£yakƒÅra then quotes instances where the word ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß means ‡§Ö‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø. ‡§®‡§®‡•Å ‡§ö ‡§≠‡•ã‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§ø ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‚Äî ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß ‡§ì‡§¶‡§®‡§É, ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§É ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§™‡§É, ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡•Ç‡§É ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡§æ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§ø ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•á, ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§ ‡§è‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ã ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç, ‡§® ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É

Nagojibhatta’s statement ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§ø ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§£ ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç, ‡§Ü‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§Æ‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•• 51

‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•• ‡§∏‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•á ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§π‡•á ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ã ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§£‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§á‡§π‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§§‡§¶‡•á‡§µ || F Oh Sir, the word fer is used also in connection with transient objects; Ex. ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß ‡§ì‡§¶‡§®‡§É (Food is ready); ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§É ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§™‡§É (Dhal is ready): fear : (the yavƒÅg≈´ preparation is ready). Since the word is used in connection with transient objects also, how can it be said that it means nitya and not karya? Since the word is used in the Sangraha as antonym to karya, we infer that it means nitya there; so also here. Since the word is used in Sangraha as an antonym to karya, it is but right that it means nitya there. Since there is no criterion here to decide its meaning one way or the other, MahƒÅbhƒÅ·π£yakara suggests another way to come to the same conclusion. ‡§Ö‡§•‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§ï‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§ø ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§µ‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø, ‡§Ö‡§™ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø, ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á; ‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§π‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß ‡§è‡§µ ‡§® ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•• Or even single words have the restrictive sense. Ex. rer: and ar. They respectively mean, ‘one who feeds himself only on water’ and one who feeds himself only on air.’ Similarly the word fe here means only fee and not sadhya. The defect that underlies this explanation is this. The words: and age are compound words, while the word fra is a single word. In splitting the compound the word which denotes restriction may be brought in. Such is not the case with single words. Hence MahƒÅbhƒÅ·π£yakƒÅra tries to explain it thus. ‡§Ö‡§•‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§¶‡§≤‡•ã‡§™‡•ã‡§Ω‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É - ‡§Ö‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§É ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§É, ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§≠‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•• 52 PASPASAHNIKA Or it may be considered that a word which preceded fe has been dropped, its original form being arrafe in the same way as ‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§É is the shortened form of ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§É; and ‡§≠‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ of ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø- ‡§≠‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ. The defect that underlies this explanation is this. In the case of the words ‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§É and ‡§≠‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ standing respectively for ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§É and ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ, it should be noted that ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§É and ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ are mentioned at the first instance and only later on for the sake of brevity : and war are used. The same is not the case here. Besides there is nothing to suggest that the word ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß is used here to denote ‡§Ö‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß. Hence MahabhƒÅ·π£yakƒÅra suggests the final solution thus :- ‡§Ö‡§•‡§µ‡§æ ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•á‡§∑‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§® ‡§π‡§ø ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§æ‡§¶‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§®‡•ã ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§£‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É ‡•• If so, we explain that the word fea means fa since a text cannot be thrown away on the ground that it is not clear. Its correct sense should be understood from the commentaries or the interpretation given by the commentators. ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á‡§® ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§Æ‡§π‡§§‡§æ ‡§ï‡§£‡•ç‡§†‡•á‡§® ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶ ‡§è‡§µ‡•ã‡§™‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§É, ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§Ω‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§π‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ? Why should he give room for this kind of interpretation? Why should he not, with his open mouth, have given expression to the word nitya, when there would be no ambiguity ?

What then? It is used to connote repetition also. Ex. ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§∏‡§ø‡§§‡§É (One who ever laughs) and ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§É (one who ever prattles). Since it connotes repetition also, it should be
  • ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§ï‡§æ‡§£‡§ø is another reading + ‡§Ü‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§ï‡§æ‡§£‡§ø is another reading. 5 ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡•ç‡§µ‡§≤‡§ø‡§§‡§É is another reading. + ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç is another reading. 54 PASPAS’AHNIKA free from ambiguity only by the interpretation of the commentators. The Acarya thinks that the word siddha is used at the commencement for the sake of mangala and I am able to interpret that it means nitya. Hence is the use of the word siddha and not nitya. Having thus discussed the meaning of the word fea, the author begins to deal with the statement ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•á ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á and discusses whether the word artha denotes genus or individaality. ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ’ ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•á ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§ö ’ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ? ‡§Ü‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π ‡•§ ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§ ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç ‡§Ü‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ With what meaning (genus or individuality) in mind is the compound split thus ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•á ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á ? ‘Akrti’ (genus), says he. Why so? For ƒÅkrti is nityƒÅ and dravya is anitya. ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•á ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§ö ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§π‡§ø ‡§Ö‡§•‡§µ‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•à‡§∞‡§≠‡§ø‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§É || If dravya is padartha, how is the compound split? It is split thus ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•á ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á; for, the relation of the word to its meaning is nitya, (though the meaning in the form of dravya is anitya). The author then takes the word ak·πõti to connote shape and in that case begins to deal with the nature of the splitting of the compound- ‡§Ö‡§•‡§µ‡§æ ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§è‡§µ ‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•ã‡§Ç ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ã ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•á ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§ø ; ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç, ‡§Ü‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡•§ ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ? ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§¶‡•É‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç ‡§ï‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§™‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø, ‡§™‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§æ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§Æ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ò‡§ü‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á, ‡§ò‡§ü‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§Æ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á; ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§∏‡•Å‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§£ ‡§ï‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø, ‡§™‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§æ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§Æ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ï‡§æ‡§É

‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á, ‡§∞‡•Å‡§ö‡§ï‡§æ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§Æ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§ü‡§ï‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á, ‡§ï‡§ü‡§ï‡§æ ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§Æ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡§æ‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡•Å‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§™‡§ø‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡§™‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§ñ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡§∏‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡•á ‡§ï‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§≤‡•á ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ü‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø, ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§¶‡•á‡§µ ‡•§ ‡§Ü‡§π‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§™‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§® ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§µ‡§∂‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡•• Or the compound is split thus even when the meaning of the word is dravya; for the dravya always remains the same, while the shape is changing. How is it? Thus it is seen in the world-Mud in one shape becomes a clod; it is broken and it is converted into small pots; that shape is destroyed and the same mud is made into jars. So also is gold. In one shape it is a ball; it is destroyed and the gold is converted into rings; they are destroyed and it is made into bracelets; that shape is destroyed and it is made into a kind of amulets; that being destroyed, it is made into ear-rings as bright as red-hot charcoal of ebony wood. The shape changes from one to another, but the material remains the same. Though the shape is destroyed, the material remains. ‡§Ü‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§™‡§ø ‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ã ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•á ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§®‡§®‡•Å ‡§ö‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‘‡§Ü‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ’ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§®‡•à‡§§‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§Ü‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡•§ ‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡•ç ? ‡§® ‡§ï‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§™‡§∞‡§§‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§™‡§∞‡§§‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø, ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ ‡§§‡•Å ‡§â‡§™‡§≤‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡•§‡•§ Even accepting ƒÅk·πõti to be padartha, it is but proper to split the compound thus ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•á ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á. akrti is anitya? No, it is nitya. seen at one place, it does not fail found in other objects (of the same genus). Has it not been said that How? Though it is not to exist in all places; it is NOTE. Here it should be borne in mind that akrti when it is considered to be nitya, means genus and when it is considered to be anityƒÅ, it means shape. 56 PASPAS AHNIKA ‡§Ö‡§•‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡•á‡§¶‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Ç‡§ü‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§≤‡§ø ‡§Ö‡§®‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§™‡§ú‡§®‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø ‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç ‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§¶‡§™‡§ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•§ ‡§Ü‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§™‡§ø ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡•§ Or this is not the definition of nitya:-that which is free from ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ, ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ and ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ; but that from which its inherent property is never severed is nitya. What is tattva? It-ness is tattva. The tattva is never separated from ƒÅkrti. NOTE. ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ is seen from the apparent red crystal in the proximity of red-flower. The relation of redness and crystal is anitya, since it disappears at the disappearance of the red flower. ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ is seen in the process of a fruit becoming a ripe fruit. The relation with its colour when it is not ripe disappears when it becomes ripe and hence the colour is anitya. ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ is complete destruction.

  • Cf. ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Ç‡§ü‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§π‡§§‡§æ; ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§≤‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ; ‡§Ö‡§®‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§®‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ (Pradipa). H ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§∞‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§ï‡•Ç‡§ü‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡•ç = ‡§Ü‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§ï‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§∞‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§≤‡§ø ‡§Ö‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§™‡§ú‡§®‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§∞‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡§Ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§∑‡§°‡•ç‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§£‡•ã‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞, ‡§Ö‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§®‡§æ‡§∂‡§É, ‡§â‡§™‡§ú‡§®‡§É ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç, ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§É = ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É, ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•Ä ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•á, ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§É ‡§Ö‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ø‡§É ‡§á‡§§‡§ø (Uddyotana). = = = ‡§ß‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§™‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§µ ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ñ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Ç‡§ü‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ; ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§æ‡§≤‡§É, ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§™‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ã ‡§¶‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§§‡§æ, ‡§Ö‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ; ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§É ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•å ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•å ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•å ‡§Ö‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§É; ‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§™‡§ú‡§®‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ö‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É ‡§Ö‡§®‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§Æ‡§É ‡§Ö‡§™‡§ö‡§Ø‡§É; ‡§Ö‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§∑‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§æ‡§∂ (Uddy√∂ta). It deserves to be noted that Nag≈çjibhatta has not given the meaning of ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø both he and Annambhatta differ in the meanings of the words ‡§Ö‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø, ‡§â‡§™‡§ú‡§® and ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø. 3 ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§É = Birth ; ‡§â‡§™‡§ú‡§®‡§É = Existence or stability; ‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§É = Growth; ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§É = Transformation; ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ø‡§É - Reduction; ‡§Ö‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡§É = Destruction.

[[7]]

‡§Ö‡§•‡§µ‡§æ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§è‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§á‡§¶‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡§¶‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§∑ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‚Äî ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•á ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡•• Or what is the use of this discussion that one is nitya and the other anitya? When we take the meaning to be nitya, we split the compound thus : ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•á ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•á. ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§É ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§ø ? ‘‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§§‡§É ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§§‡•á, ‡§®‡•à‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•å ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡•á ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§≠‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§É ‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•å ‡•§ ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§®‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡•á, ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§ò‡§ü‡•á‡§® ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡§≠‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§π ‚Äì ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å ‡§ò‡§ü‡§Ç, ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§ï‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§® ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ï‡§∞‡§£‡§ï‡•Å‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ü‡§π ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§§‡•á ‡•§ How is it understood that sabda, artha and sambandha are nitya? From the world. For words are used to denote objects and no effort is made to Coin them. Effort is taken in creating such things as are karya. For instance he who has the use of a pot goes to the potter’s house and says, ‚Ä¢ Make a pot; I have to use it. But no one similarly goes to the house of a grammarian and says, ‘Coin words; I shall make use of them.’ He thinks of the object and makes use of words denoting them. ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø ‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï ‡§è‡§∑‡•Å ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç, ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ! ‘‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É ’ ‡•§ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§§‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É, ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É ‡§ß‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É, ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ú‡§®‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É 11 If then the world is the authority for the use of words, what purpose is served by the Vyakarana sastra? When words ‡§è‡§∑‡•Å ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§∑‡•Å is another reading. 58 PASPAS’AHNIKA are used in the sense in which each is current in the world, injunction to use the correct word is made by the sastra for the sake of dharma. Dharma-niyama, what does it mean? It means niyama for dharma, niyama for the sake of dharma and niyama having for its fruit dharma. NOTE. It deserves to be noted that KƒÅiyata clearly says that the compound dharma-niyama·∏• should be split only as dharmasya niyamah. If so, Mahabha·π£yakara does not mention how the compound is split, but brings out the sense of the compound. All the three ways mentioned there -‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É, ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É and ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ú‡§®‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É may be taken to mean the same. The only difference is that the second is more explanatory than the first and the third is more explanatory than the second. What is, then, the meaning of dharma? It may be interpreted in three ways: 1. ‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ Cf. ‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§£‡•ã ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§É ‡§™‡§°‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•ã ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§Ø‡§É ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö (M. B. I. 1, 1). 2. ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ Cf. ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡•á ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§∏ ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É ‡•§ (M. B. I, 1, 1). 3. ‡§Ö‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç Cf. ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§É ‡•§ ( M. B. I, 1, 1). Nag≈çjibha·π≠·π≠a says (as the opinion of some) that in a fagm: ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ has the first meaning, in ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É it has the second meaning and in as a far: it has the third meaning. But it is better to take that it has all the three meanings in each. ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§≤‡•å‡§ï‡§ø‡§ï‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡•§ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§¶‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É, ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡•á ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§≤‡•å‡§ï‡§ø‡§ï‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§•‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§ ‡§è‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§É, ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§≤‡•å‡§ï‡§ø‡§ï‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ö ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡•§ ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§ï‡•Å‡§ü, ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Ç‡§ï‡§∞ Cf. Bodhayana Dharmasutra 1, 12, 1.

‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§≤‡§§‡§ø‡§ò‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á, ‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡§™‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§π‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç, ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§á‡§¶‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§ñ‡•á‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∑‡•Å ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø, ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§ñ‡•á‡§¶‡§µ‡§ø‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§Ö‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§á‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§á‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§ó‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•• As in laukika and vaidika incidentst. The Southerners are fond of using words with taddhita suffixes (without special significance). They, instead of using ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á and ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡•á, use ‡§≤‡•å‡§ï‡§ø‡§ï‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï‡•á‡§∑‡•Å. Or it is but proper that the taddhita suffix has a meaning. The term fag may be taken to mean ‡§≤‡•å‡§ï‡§ø‡§ï‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ö ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡•Å. There is with reference to the worldly incident, the saying that the domestic cock should not be eaten nor the domestic pig; food is taken to remove. hunger; it may be removed by any one even with dogs’ meat; there is the restriction made that one is eatable and the other is non-eatable. Similarly man meets woman to satisfy his sexual passion; it may be had in meeting any woman deserving or non-deserving; there is the restriction made that one is meet-able and the other is non-meet-able. NOTE. The mention of the word for suggests that Katyayana was a Southerner, while both the SutrakƒÅra and the Bhasyakara were Northerners. Some think that there is a little sneer here. ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡•á ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§ø ‡§™‡§Ø‡•ã‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ã ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§£‡§É, ‡§Ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§ó‡•Ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É, ‡§Ü‡§Æ‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§®‡§§‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ; ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§Ö‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á; ‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§∂‡§æ‡§≤‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§ø ‡§ã‡§§‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç ; ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§¨‡•à‡§≤‡•ç‡§µ‡§É ‡§ñ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§™‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ; f The expression ‡§≤‡•å‡§ï‡§ø‡§ï‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï‡•á‡§∑‡•Å is taken to mean in the smrti and ≈õruti texts by Kaiya·π≠a and others. But on viewing this with pit it is better to take it in the sense ‘in the incidents of the world and V√©dic rituals.’ In that case ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É is understood after ‡§≤‡•å‡§ï‡§ø‡§ï‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡§ø‡§ï‡•á‡§∑‡•Å. 60 PASPAS’AHNIKA ‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§®‡•Å‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ; ‡§∂‡§ï‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§® ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡•á‡§µ ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡§∂‡•Å‡§∞‡§®‡•Å‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§§‡§•‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•å ‡§ï‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§ß‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ - ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á - ‡§≠‡•É‡§ó‡•Ç‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡§æ ‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§á‡§§‡§ø; ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•á‡§£‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡§π‡§®‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§ï‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§™‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§ö ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‚Äî ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡§Ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡•• 9 So with reference to the Vedic rituals it is said that during austerities BrƒÅhma·πáa, if hungry, may take milk, K·π£attriya Yavagu, and Vaisya curd of milk and whey; Vrata intends only food; Rice and meat may serve the same purpose; still restriction is made. So also it is said that the stake to which the sacrificial animal is tied should be of bilva tree or khadira tree; the stake is intended to tie the sacrificial animal; any piece of wood standing upright or otherwise may serve the purpose; there is the restriction made. Similarly kapala’s-small pieces of mud-are put in fire and the mantra which means, Heat them with the intense heat of Bhrgus and Angiras’ is pronounced; the small pieces will be heated whether the mantra is recited or not; there is the restriction made that, if it is done so, it begets merit. ‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§π‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§µ‡§ó‡§§‡•å ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§® ‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§® ‡§ö ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•ã‡§Ω‡§≠‡§ø‡§ß‡•á‡§Ø‡•ã, ‡§®‡§æ‡§™‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§® ‡§á‡§§‡§ø; ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§¶‡§Ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§ø ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡•• So here also though the meaning is understood both from the correct word and the corrupt one, still restriction is made that meaning is to be made out only from the correct word, since from it alone accrues merit. The meaning of the first varttika having been fully explained, there arises a doubt whether word that is not current in the world is correct or not, since it has been said there that it is used only in such meanings as are current in the world.

‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É-

‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡•à ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ; ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ, ‡§ä‡§∑ ‡§§‡•á‡§∞‡•á ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§™‡•á‡§ö ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ Is but not current-there are evidently words which are not current ; viz, ≈´sa, tera, cakra, peca. ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Æ‡§§‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ? What if there are words not current ? ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§õ‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ø ‡§á‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Ä ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡§µ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É ‡•§ ‡§á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Æ‡•ç - ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡•à ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø, ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É, ‡§Ö‡§•‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§® ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ö ‡§Ö‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Æ‡•ç ‡•• For only from usage you determine the correctness of words. Those which are not now in usage cannot be correct. This is at first contradictory to say that there are words but they are not in usage; if they are, they cannot have fallen out of use, and if they have fallen out of use, they cannot exist; they exist but they are not in use is contradictory. ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§æ‡§® ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•Å ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§π ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡•á‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§ï‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§É ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ? 9 You use the words and say at the same time that they are out of use. Who else of your type can make correct use of words? ‡§®‡•à‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Æ‡•ç ‚Äî ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§¶‡•ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§Æ‡§É * ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§É ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§ß‡§§‡•á ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ç‡§Æ‡§É, ‡§Ø‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á ‡§Ö‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§ï‡§•‡•á‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§ï‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§É ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡•á ‡§∏‡§æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§ø, ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ This is not contradictory; we first say that they exist since they are formed from the rules of grammar; then Note the use of the plural by the pupil. This shows that he has lost his balance. 62 PASPAS’AHNIKA we say that they are not in use since they are not used in the world. As regards the statement-who else of your type can make correct use of words?-we do not say that they are not used by us. ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø ? What then? ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á ‡§Ö‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø. They are not made use of in the world. ‡§®‡§®‡•Å ‡§ö ‡§≠‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•ã ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á ? Are not you one in the world ? ‡§Ö‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á, ‡§® ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§É ‡•§ I am one in the world, but not the whole world. * ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ö‡•á‡§®‡•ç‡§®, ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ‡§§‡•ç– ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡•ç ‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§® ‡•§ ‡§ï‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‚Äî ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á, ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ö‡•à‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§•‡§æ‡§É ‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡•• “Is but not current " cannot be said, for words are used to express ideas. If it is said, “Is but not current,” it can be denied. How? On account of the use of words to express ideas-words are used to express ideas and there are ideas, to express which the words are used. ‡§Ö‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç- ‡§Ö‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§É ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ó‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç, ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§õ‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§§‡•á ; ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ, ‡§ä‡§™‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§µ ‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•Å‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É, ‡§§‡•á‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§ï ‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§É, ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§ï ‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É, ‡§™‡•á‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡•á ‡§ï‡•ç‡§µ ‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡•§ He suggests that he uses such words to denote the form of the word, while ordinary people use words only to express ideas. The objection raised is successfully met by five reasons:(1) arthe sabdaprayogat, (2) aprayogah prayƒÅgƒÅnyateal. (3) aprayukte dirghasattravat, (4) sarve desantare and (5) vede.

Non-use on account of the use of other (synonymous) expressions-It is but proper that these words are not in use. Why? On account of other expressions-since other expressions are used to convey the idea of these words, viz. ‚Ä¢ Kva y≈´yam usitah’ in place of ‘asa’ Icva yuyam tirnal in place of ’tera,’ ‘kva y≈´yam krtavantah’ in place of * cakra’ and ’ kva yuyam pakvavantah’ in place of ‘peca.’ ‡§Ö‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§ò‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§§‡•ç ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§§‡§•‡§æ‡§™‡§ø ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§ò‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§≤‡•ç‡§≤‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡•á‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡•§ ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§¶‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§ò‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§∂‡§§‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§ö ‡§® ‡§ö‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§ï‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§¶‡§™‡§ø ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§µ‡§π‡§∞‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•á‡§µ‡§≤‡§Æ‡•É‡§∑‡§ø‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡•§ ‡§ß‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§É ‡§∂‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡§ß‡§§‡•á ‡•§ Though not current, to be treated like dirghasattraThough they are not current, yet they should certainly be treated in grammar like dirghasattra. Dirghasattras are sacrifices performed in one hundred or one thousand days and they are not performed now-a-days. Still YƒÅj√±ika’s enjoin them in the chapters dealing with sacrifices in the Vedas since it is considered that their study is a nityakarma.¬ß ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•á‚Äî ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§ñ‡§≤‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•á ‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á All in other places-All of these words are certainly in use in other places. ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§∂‡§¨‡•ç‡§¶‡§É ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡§∏‡§™‡§∞ (Nagojibhatta)
